< Review>
Rude. All around unpleasant. I walked in for a simple full acrylic set ($26 on their menu) 'Tim' didn't speak one word to me through the whole experience, but he spoke to the women around me while they were getting their nails done. Every time I pointed out a concern with my nail he'd tell me not to worry, it would be filed out....I'm a paying customer, if my nails aren't even you should be understanding and fix the issue. Instead no matter how many times I said 'oh...the acrylic doesn't completely cover this nail' or 'are you sure it's not supposed to cover my whole nail?' He'd just tell me it's all fine it will be filed out. Not to mention how frustrated he would get at ME because I accidentally touched the inside of the OPI nail light box (which I'd never used before so I had no idea there was a small lip) he would continuously HUFF as he fixed it...but at lease he 'fixed' it.
I left there after paying $35, yes THIRTY-FIVE DOLLARS, and went somewhere else to have my nails fixed because I had nail polish all over the underside, acrylic stuck under my nails and on my fingers and it felt so rushed like I was inconveniencing them.
I won't go back. I hope others don't waste their time. The Anderson Walmart has an AMAZING nail salon and amazing people who work there! Please don't waste your money at this nail salon.</Review>

< Review>

Depending on my needs and those of my clients, will determine what assets I required from the storage. The efficiencies of having one unit organized with racks surrounding the entry that's result in the ability for my team members and myself to be able to efficiently leverage our organizational infrastructure in my new 10 x 10 space. < review>
If you want a delicious, filling, three-course meal for two, this is the place to go!

Start with an order of the Spring Rolls. These rolls come with a delicious peanut sauce that adds a kick. Next, is the fried Calamari. Yet another dish, for two, dipped in a tangy, mildly-spicy green herb sauce.

For the main plate, split the Pineapple Chicken Curry, which goes excellent when drizzled over the Pineapple fried rice, and enjoy the plethora of delicious, mouth-watering, spice and flavor.

For an even fuller experience, order a milk tea with boba to go along with your meal.

Excellent food and excellent service!<//review>

<date>1617234266526<//date><rate>1< /rate>< review>
If I could do zero I would. Nothing against the day to day workers at the post, the managers set them up to fail.

A package "arrived" at my address the other day. I was at work, but my partner was home. When I received the delivery notification it was marked that my package had been delivered to an individual, so I assumed that mean the one in my residence. I also assumed it meant the package had not been left outside on my doorstep, as that is a separate button. Well because it was marked in that manner I didn't think I would need to check in with my partner to see if she could retrieve it from the porch, as it was marked as delivered to an individual.

Because of the amount of time my package remained on my doorstep, even though I live in a gated residence currently with no immediate neighbors in the courtyard complex, the package was stolen. I don't know who stole the package, really the postman could have stolen the package if he wanted to, as I learned later. I went to file an insurance claim, and was told there was nothing to be done for me by a woman who claimed to be the supervisor. If she was the supervisor it was clear she had not been trained to be the supervisor because her customer service skills were less than negligible, she claimed it wasn't their responsibility as the package had been "delivered". I'm not contesting whether or not they attempted to deliver it. What I am saying is they fed me misinformation that resulted in the package being stolen, if they didn't steal it themselves. The salt of it all is they make you pay extra to insure packages, and if the insurance isn't covering human error and incidentals on their end what on earth is it covering?

This really is the equivalent of someone telling you to turn around then tossing you a ball, and when it crashes into your head turning it around on you are saying "Well why didn't you catch it?"

Avoid the USPS if this is your main post office.< /review>

<pictures>None< /pictures><Text>Overall, I am beyond impressed by the level of professionalism and care I have received from the Sunnyvale branch. The fact that I have a point of contact to help with my business needs is above and beyond my expectations of working with USPS.

My driver, in particular, has made my life as a startup business owner so much easier. I moved my business to Sunnyvale from Los Angeles in April and expected to hire someone dedicated to fulfillment, shipping, and making drop-offs at USPS and FedEx. I didn't end up needing to hire someone because of how responsive and accommodating USPS and my driver has been. For a new business with a limited budget this has been huge. It means that I can dedicate more time to getting the word out about my business and developing new products.

Our regular driver offered me his personal cell phone number so that I can communicate with him on a daily basis. He suggested this after I had scheduled a recurring pickup daily (to save myself the time and effort scheduling pickups) but only had packages 4/6 days a week. Now, I make it a point to text him daily with the updated status. If there are no packages, he's off the hook and can save time. If I have more packages that day, he can tell his manager that there is a large pickup and send a 2nd truck. It works so well and I have enjoyed getting to know my USPS driver. It almost feels like how I imagine the 1950s to be when the mailman is part of your daily routine and adds to your sense of community. He asks questions about my business and I feel like he genuinely cares about our success. He even lets me know when he's finishing up in the building's mail room so that I can hurry up and finish preparing orders. When I was on vacation last week he texted a photo to reassure me that FedEx had picked up my packages so that I could have peace on mind! This is a level of service that is unheard of!

I felt like giving this feedback because my impression is that USPS only receives negative feedback from customers. I have seen drastic improvements in the operations and professionalism of USPS over the years and I think this story deserves to be told. It kind of reminds me of the Domino's re-branding when they drastically improved their product/service. Keep up the good work!</Text>< rate>

Then said, "okay so you're telling me your office is refusing me service because I can't wear a mask?"  She said yes. I said is your office manager here and she said well we have a sign on the door saying it's required. I replied, still calm and polite, "I'm sorry but I still can not wear a mask I don't think you understand, it's not that I just don't want to,  I can not. I literally waited two hours in the lobby and then another hour and fifty five minutes in the exam room. When I was in the exam room my throat was swabbed for strep and no one came back for almost two hours. NO COMMUNICATION from anyone. When I was finally seen by a physician, he offered no apology for such a long wait, proceeded to ask me a few questions and told me that I tested negative for strep. He said that he doubted I had mono but would test me anyway. The medical assistant came back to test me for mono and made a joke. How funny these people have time for jokes but no time to take ten seconds to communicate with people about what to expect. The physician then told me I tested negative for mono and that I have a respiratory infection. He didn't even use a stethoscope to check my lungs or anything.
